## Domain Knowledge
**Domain**: chemical reaction kinetics (rate laws / concentration-time ODEs)
**Analysis**: The target dA_dt is the time-derivative of a chemical species concentration A, so the task is to infer a kinetic rate law (possibly time-dependent) governing A(t). Typical structures express consumption/production rates as functions of A (reaction order, saturation, reversibility) and sometimes explicit t-dependence (changing conditions, forcing).

**Common formula structures** (built-in generic + LLM domain-specific):
- Arrhenius equation: k = c0 * exp(c1 / T) (chemical reaction rate dependence on temperature)
- Coulomb's / Newton's inverse-square law: F = c0 / r**2 (gravitational or electrostatic force)
- Stefan-Boltzmann law: P = c0 * T**4 (blackbody radiation power vs temperature)
- Beer-Lambert law: I = c0 * exp(c1 * x) (light intensity attenuation through a medium)
- Michaelis-Menten kinetics: v = c0 * S / (S + c1) (enzyme-catalyzed reaction saturation)
- Hill equation: y = c0 * x**c1 / (x**c1 + c2) (cooperative binding, sigmoidal dose-response)
- Kepler's third law: T**2 = c0 * a**3 (orbital period vs semi-major axis)
- Newton's law of cooling: T = c0 + c1 * exp(c2 * t) (exponential thermal relaxation)
- Clausius-Clapeyron relation: log(P) = c0 + c1 / T (vapor pressure vs temperature)
- Langmuir adsorption isotherm: theta = c0 * P / (1 + c1 * P) (surface adsorption equilibrium)
- Freundlich isotherm: q = c0 * C**c1 (empirical adsorption on heterogeneous surface)
- Stokes' drag: F = c0 * r * v (viscous drag force on a sphere in fluid)
- Logistic growth: N = c0 / (1 + c1 * exp(c2 * t)) (population dynamics with carrying capacity)
- Planck-Wien approximation: I = c0 * f**3 * exp(c1 * f / T) (thermal radiation spectrum)
- Zero-order consumption: dA_dt = -c0 (rate independent of A; e.g., surface-limited or constant input removal)
- First-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A (unimolecular decay, radioactive-like, simple first-order kinetics)
- Second-order decay: dA_dt = -c0 * A**2 (bimolecular/self-reaction or effective second-order behavior)
- General power-law (nth-order) rate: dA_dt = -c0 * A**c1 (empirical order fitting over concentration range)
- Parallel pathways (mixed orders): dA_dt = -c0 * A - c1 * A**2 (simultaneous first- and second-order consumption channels)
- Reversible relaxation to equilibrium: dA_dt = -c0 * A + c0 * c1 (net rate proportional to deviation from equilibrium A_eq = c1)
- Autocatalytic / self-limiting production-consumption: dA_dt = c0 * A * (c1 - A) (autocatalysis with depletion/limitation)
- Saturating (limited-site/transport-limited) consumption: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (A + c1) (rate approaches -c0 for large A)
- Time-varying first-order (accelerating conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(c1 * t) * A (rate constant increases with time)
- Time-varying first-order (deactivating conditions): dA_dt = -c0 * exp(-c1 * t) * A (effective rate constant decays with time)
- Periodic forcing (e.g., light modulation): dA_dt = -c0 * (1 + c1 * sin(c2 * t)) * A (time-periodic modulation of rate constant)
- CSTR-like source plus first-order loss: dA_dt = c0 - c1 * A (approach to steady state A_ss = c0/(c1) structurally; reactor/feed dynamics)
- Induction / ramp-up of activity: dA_dt = -c0 * A * (1 - exp(-c1 * t)) (rate starts near 0 and turns on over time)
- Sigmoidal activation of kinetics: dA_dt = -c0 * A / (1 + exp(-c1 * (t - c2))) (smooth switch-on around t ≈ c2)

**Formula structure heuristic features**:
- Oscillation damping envelope → Exponential decay envelope f(x)*exp(-c*Abs(x)) for symmetric damped oscillation, Gaussian envelope f(x)*exp(-c*x**2) for localized wave packets
- Saturation/clipping effects → Rational fraction x/(1+x), tanh; for variables with alternating positive/negative in oscillatory systems, selectively apply Abs
- Growth/decay → Exponential growth exp(c*t), Logistic 1/(1+exp(-c*x)), power law x**c
- Threshold/activation behavior → Max(x-c, 0), piecewise functions
- Coupling/cross effects → Product terms between variables x*y, power-law coupling x**c1 * y**c2
- Net consumption of A typically implies dA_dt < 0 for A > 0; sign and monotonicity constraints can rule out many candidate forms.
- Reaction order identification: log(-dA_dt) vs log(A) approximately linear suggests dA_dt ≈ -c0 * A**c1 with slope c1.
- Multiple mechanisms often appear as additive rate terms (e.g., -c0*A - c1*A**2), reflecting parallel reaction channels.
- Reversibility/equilibrium shows up as a linear offset: rates proportional to (A - A_eq) lead to dA_dt = -c0*A + c0*c1 and a nonzero steady state.
- Transport or site limitation produces saturating dependence on A, commonly captured by rational forms like A/(A+c1) where increasing A yields diminishing rate increases.
- Explicit t-dependence in the rate constant (exp(c*t), sin(c*t)) indicates changing external conditions (temperature program, illumination, catalyst activation/deactivation).
- Autocatalysis is indicated by an initial rate that increases with A and can create accelerating dynamics; self-limitation introduces a (c1 - A) factor and yields a peak then decline.
- Induction periods are suggested when dA_dt is near 0 at early t despite nonzero A; multiplicative ramp factors like (1-exp(-c*t)) capture this behavior.
- Approach to a steady state under continuous input/removal is characterized by affine kinetics c0 - c1*A, giving exponential relaxation in A(t).
